<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">Meteorological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Betsy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Betsy_1965_track.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="718" data-file-width="1024" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Betsy_1965_track.png/220px-Betsy_1965_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Betsy_1965_track.png/330px-Betsy_1965_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Betsy_1965_track.png/440px-Betsy_1965_track.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Betsy_1965_track.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map plotting the track and intensity of the storm, according to the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The origins of Hurricane Betsy can be traced back to an <a href="/wiki/Convection" title="Convection">area of disturbed weather</a> southwest of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> that first identified via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TIROS" title="TIROS">TIROS</a> <a href="/wiki/Satellite_imagery" title="Satellite imagery">satellite imagery</a> on August 23.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> Tracking westward, the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> was intercepted by a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hunters" title="Hurricane Hunters">reconnaissance airplane</a> early on August 27,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup> which concluded that the disturbance had become a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a> of moderate intensity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-1_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-1-4">[3]</a></sup> Based on information from the flight, it was estimated that the system had organized into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_depression" title="Tropical depression">tropical depression</a> by 0000 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on August 27,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> 350 mi (560 km) east-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> Although operationally the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">United States Weather Bureau</a> office in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a> upgraded the disturbance to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" title="Tropical storm">tropical storm</a> intensity three hours after their first tropical cyclone bulletin that same day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[nb 2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-1_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-1-4">[3]</a></sup> post-analysis indicated that the tropical depression had remained at the same intensity up until 1200 UTC on August 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> Nonetheless, the tropical cyclone was given the name Betsy for a period of time as a tropical depression,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup> contrary to typical <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">tropical cyclone naming</a> procedure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCNATL_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCNATL-8">[6]</a></sup> As Betsy approached the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a>, it began to move in a more northwesterly direction,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-1_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-1-4">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-2_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-2-9">[7]</a></sup> and was briefly located in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> during the overnight hours of August 28 before re-emerging into the Atlantic Ocean the following day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-2_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-2-9">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-3_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-3-10">[8]</a></sup> after which Betsy was upgraded to tropical storm classification in post-analysis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Betsy_from_TIROS_IX_Spac0008-repair.jpg"><img alt="Grayscale image of a tropical cyclone as viewed from space. Due to the position of the camera, the tropical cyclone is at center-right, with banding features visible. As a result of the camera angle, the limb of the Earth is clearly visible; outer space appears a uniform dark gray." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1213" data-file-width="1250" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Betsy_from_TIROS_IX_Spac0008-repair.jpg/220px-Betsy_from_TIROS_IX_Spac0008-repair.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Betsy_from_TIROS_IX_Spac0008-repair.jpg/330px-Betsy_from_TIROS_IX_Spac0008-repair.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Betsy_from_TIROS_IX_Spac0008-repair.jpg/440px-Betsy_from_TIROS_IX_Spac0008-repair.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Betsy_from_TIROS_IX_Spac0008-repair.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Betsy antecedent to being upgraded to hurricane intensity on August 29.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Upon moving to the northwest of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>, Betsy entered conditions favorable for marked development. An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper-level_low" title="Upper-level low">upper-level</a> <a href="/wiki/Trough_(meteorology)" title="Trough (meteorology)">trough</a> centered a short distance north of the tropical storm enhanced <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> conditions and speed <a href="/wiki/Aeroelasticity" title="Aeroelasticity">divergence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> Under these conditions, Betsy proceeded to quickly intensify,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> and reconnaissance missions tasked by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[nb 3]</a></sup> and Weather Bureau indicated that the tropical storm had reached hurricane intensity by 0000 UTC on August 30,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> centered roughly 200 mi (320 km) north-northeast of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. By coincidence, forecast responsibilities were transferred to the Weather Bureau Office in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" title="Miami, Florida">Miami, Florida</a> at the same time;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup> however, the hurricane was still under the purview of the Weather Bureau per se.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-3_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-3-10">[8]</a></sup> Due to increasing <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">atmospheric pressure</a> <a href="/wiki/Geopotential_height" title="Geopotential height">heights</a> to the north,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> Betsy drastically slowed in forward speed and intensification,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> and remained stationary for a period of time on August 31 before it began to drift westward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-4_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-4-13">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-5_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-5-14">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-6_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-6-15">[12]</a></sup> On September 2, Betsy began to quickly intensify,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-7_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-7-16">[13]</a></sup> and after strengthening to a Category 3 hurricane-equivalent – a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales" title="Tropical cyclone scales">major hurricane</a> on the modern-day <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson hurricane wind scale">Saffir–Simpson hurricane wind scale</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[nb 4]</a></sup> – the small hurricane attained Category 4 intensity and reached an initial peak intensity with winds of 140 mph (220 km/h) at 0000 UTC on September 4, while situated well north of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turks_and_Caicos" title="Turks and Caicos">Turks and Caicos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-7"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-11_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-11-19">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, on September 5, a <a href="/wiki/Block_(meteorology)" title="Block (meteorology)">blocking ridge</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_pressure_area" title="High pressure area">high pressure</a> situated over the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_United_States" title="Eastern United States">Eastern United States</a> forced Betsy to make a tight,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-13_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-13-20">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-16_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-16-21">[17]</a></sup> clockwise loop and track in an unusual southwesterly path, redirecting it towards <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup> At roughly the same time, the hurricane weakened to Category 2 intensity, though it later restrengthened to Category 3 intensity on September 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-8"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> Betsy's atypical southwesterly path brought it directly over several islands in the northern Bahamas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-8"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup> including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Abaco_Island" title="Great Abaco Island">Great Abaco Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-19_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-19-22">[18]</a></sup> After stalling for a third time over portions of the central Bahamas, the major hurricane resumed its prior westward track towards <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">South Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-6"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-9"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-9"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-24_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-24-23">[19]</a></sup> Early on September 8,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-27_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-27-24">[20]</a></sup> Betsy made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> on <a href="/wiki/Key_Largo" title="Key Largo">Key Largo</a> in extreme southeastern Florida with winds of 125 mph (205 km/h) and a minimum <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barometric_pressure" title="Barometric pressure">barometric pressure</a> of 953 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>; 28.15 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inches_of_mercury" title="Inches of mercury">inHg</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-2_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2-25">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-10"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> Without much change in strength,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-11"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> the intense hurricane quickly traversed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Keys" title="Upper Keys">Upper Keys</a> and <a href="/wiki/Florida_Bay" title="Florida Bay">Florida Bay</a> before emerging midday on September 8 into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-7"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-28_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-28-26">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Situated in the warm waters of the Gulf of Mexico on September 8,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-2_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2-25">[21]</a></sup> Betsy began to strengthen and accelerate towards the west and then northwest,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-12"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> under the influence of the same <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">ridge</a> of high pressure that had forced it southwestward three days prior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-8"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> At roughly the same time, hurricane forecast operations were handed over the Weather Bureau Office in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Orleans,_Louisiana" title="New Orleans, Louisiana">New Orleans, Louisiana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-30_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-30-27">[23]</a></sup> During its trek through the gulf, Betsy accelerated to a maximum forward speed of 22 mph (35 km/h), a speed anomalously high for a tropical cyclone traversing the Gulf of Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-9"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> At 0600 UTC on September 9, the hurricane was estimated to have regained Category 4 intensity, and continued to strengthen as it neared the Central <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Gulf_Coast" title="United States Gulf Coast">United States Gulf Coast</a>. At 0000 UTC the next day, Betsy reached its primary peak intensity with winds of 155 mph (250 km/h) and a minimum central pressure of 941 mbar (hPa; 27.79 inHg) shortly before moving ashore a rural area of Louisiana coastline adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Houma,_Louisiana" title="Houma, Louisiana">Houma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Isle,_Louisiana" title="Grand Isle, Louisiana">Grand Isle</a> early on September 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-2_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2-25">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAHurricanes_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-LAHurricanes-28">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-13"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> Once inland, Betsy quickly weakened,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-2_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2-25">[21]</a></sup> and paralleled the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> before degenerating into a tropical depression by 0600 UTC the following day. Afterwards, it began to track northeastward along the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a> before it transitioned into an <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> on September 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-14"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> The remnant extratropical circulation of Betsy persisted into southern <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> before dissipating entirely by 0000 UTC on September 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPCRain_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-WPCRain-29">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-15"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparations">Preparations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Betsy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Preparations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="The_Bahamas,_Cuba,_and_Florida"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bahamas.2C_Cuba.2C_and_Florida">The Bahamas, Cuba, and Florida</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Betsy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The Bahamas, Cuba, and Florida">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Betsy_analysis_9_Sep_1965.png"><img alt="Contoured map of a tropical cyclone in a body of water. Contours denote isobars, and the location of the storm is marked with a tropical cyclone symbol." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="535" data-file-width="628" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hurricane_Betsy_analysis_9_Sep_1965.png/300px-Hurricane_Betsy_analysis_9_Sep_1965.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hurricane_Betsy_analysis_9_Sep_1965.png/450px-Hurricane_Betsy_analysis_9_Sep_1965.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Hurricane_Betsy_analysis_9_Sep_1965.png/600px-Hurricane_Betsy_analysis_9_Sep_1965.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Betsy_analysis_9_Sep_1965.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Surface weather analysis map of Betsy on September 8</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral" title="Cape Canaveral">Cape Kennedy</a>, <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> delayed the erection of an <a href="/wiki/Atlas-Centaur" title="Atlas-Centaur">Atlas-Centaur</a> rocket which was to be used to launch a craft towards the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> as part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surveyor_Program" title="Surveyor Program">Surveyor Program</a> on September 2. Several other prepared rockets on the site's launch pads were readied for potential emergency scramble should the hurricane impact the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GoldCoastLeery_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-GoldCoastLeery-30">[26]</a></sup> Other American space personnel stationed in <a href="/wiki/Grand_Turk_Island" title="Grand Turk Island">Grand Turk Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mayaguana" title="Mayaguana">Mayaguana</a> began preparatory measures after the United States Air Force issued a No. 1 alert for the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RagingNearBahamas_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-RagingNearBahamas-31">[27]</a></sup> Personnel from a small outpost on Allan Cay were evacuated to <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bahama" title="Grand Bahama">Grand Bahama</a>, despite indications at the time that Betsy would curve away from the Bahamas or the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast of the United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FicklyBetsy_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FicklyBetsy-32">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AimsAtCarolina_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-AimsAtCarolina-33">[29]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Brunswick,_Georgia" title="Brunswick, Georgia">Brunswick, Georgia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Glynco" title="Naval Air Station Glynco">Naval Air Station Glynco</a>, 21 jet <a href="/wiki/Fighter-bomber" title="Fighter-bomber">fighter-bombers</a> were evacuated inland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RelentlessBetsy_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-RelentlessBetsy-34">[30]</a></sup> On September 4, helicopters arrived at the <a href="/wiki/Frying_Pan_Shoals_Light" title="Frying Pan Shoals Light">Frying Pan Shoals Light</a> to evacuate the lighthouse's operators due to the impending threat of a hurricane strike.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-500MiSC_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-500MiSC-35">[31]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="Palm Beach, Florida">Palm Beach</a> area, a group composed of regional <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">Red Cross</a> disaster chairman Forest W. Dana and nearby town officials held a nearly nonstop radio vigil service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBNoChance_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBNoChance-36">[32]</a></sup> Red Cross volunteers in <a href="/wiki/The_Carolinas" title="The Carolinas">The Carolinas</a> set up three district headquarters to prepare shelters, first aid programs, and communications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyStalls_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyStalls-37">[33]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relief_agency" title="Relief agency">relief agency</a> also readied seven first aid and food vans in the cities of <a href="/wiki/New_Bern,_North_Carolina" title="New Bern, North Carolina">New Bern</a> and Wilmington in North Carolina and <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_South_Carolina" title="Charleston, South Carolina">Charleston, South Carolina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ThreatensBahamasFlorida_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-ThreatensBahamasFlorida-38">[34]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">United States Department of Agriculture</a> prepared food supplies in the event of an emergency for the two states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyStalls_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyStalls-37">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Betsy stalled and assumed a southwesterly course towards southern Florida, precautionary measures ceased in the Carolinas but were initiated in Florida and The Bahamas. <a href="/wiki/Mackey_Airlines" title="Mackey Airlines">Mackey Airlines</a> assisted in the evacuation of 227 residents of West End Island to Miami, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">Fort Lauderdale</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">West Palm Beach, Florida</a>, over the course of three flights. Three additional <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-6" title="Douglas DC-6">Douglas DC-6</a> airliners from Mackey Airlines evacuated 240 people, primarily American tourists, from <a href="/wiki/Nassau_County,_Florida" title="Nassau County, Florida">Nassau</a> to Miami. Various commercial flights between the archipelago and Florida were cancelled due to the impending storm. In Florida, various relief agencies prepared 9,000 hot dogs, 8,000 hamburgers, and 6,000 servings of chicken, to be donated to local hospitals and charitable organizations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WarningsExpected_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-WarningsExpected-39">[35]</a></sup> The United States Weather Bureau urged for the reopening of grocery stores and lumbers yards which had been closed for <a href="/wiki/Labor_Day" title="Labor Day">Labor Day</a> in order to increase availability of hurricane preparedness materials to potentially affected populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SwingSW_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-SwingSW-40">[36]</a></sup> In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Downtown_Miami" title="Downtown Miami">downtown Miami</a>, a traffic coordination plan for the evacuation of vehicles and aquatic craft through the <a href="/wiki/Brickell_Avenue_Bridge" title="Brickell Avenue Bridge">Brickell Avenue Bridge</a> was set in place. <a href="/wiki/Homestead_Air_Reserve_Base" title="Homestead Air Reserve Base">Homestead Air Reserve Base</a> went into Phase 2 of its hurricane preparedness plan, in which aircraft stationed at the base were serviced for potential evacuation to bases in <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BridgePlanBetsy_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-BridgePlanBetsy-41">[37]</a></sup> Upon Betsy's recurvature southwestward toward the peninsula on September 7, the Weather Bureau strongly advised evacuation procedures between Fort Lauderdale and Key Largo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyAimsFury_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyAimsFury-42">[38]</a></sup> Evacuation was strongly advised in the Florida Keys, where rising water as a result of the storm could potentially flood over portions of <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 1 in Florida">U.S. Route 1</a> – the only primary access route from the Keys to the mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyAimingFloridaSpokane_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyAimingFloridaSpokane-43">[39]</a></sup> Overall, an estimated 50,000 residents were within coastal regions where evacuations were advised. The U.S. Navy abandoned its housing project on Big Pine Key to avoid the hurricane, while sheriff deputies in Marathon, Tavernier, and <a href="/wiki/Islamorada,_Florida" title="Islamorada, Florida">Islamorada</a> strongly advised evacuation in those respective cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ShredsMiami_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-ShredsMiami-44">[40]</a></sup> Various offices, businesses, and schools were closed in advance of the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyAimingFloridaSpokane_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyAimingFloridaSpokane-43">[39]</a></sup> Airlines cancelled service to Fort Lauderdale and Miami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsySpokesmanReviewFlorida_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsySpokesmanReviewFlorida-45">[41]</a></sup> In the latter, city crews dismantled traffic lights along <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biscayne_Boulevard" title="Biscayne Boulevard">Biscayne Boulevard</a>; such procedure was influenced by the damage wrought by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Cleo" title="Hurricane Cleo">Hurricane Cleo</a> a <a href="/wiki/1964_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1964 Atlantic hurricane season">year prior</a>.</p>
<p>On September 7, the United States Weather Bureau predicted that Betsy would make landfall in <a href="/wiki/Matanzas_Province" title="Matanzas Province">Matanzas Province</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BeadCuba_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-BeadCuba-46">[42]</a></sup> The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=National_Observatory_of_Cuba&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="National Observatory of Cuba (page does not exist)">National Observatory of Cuba</a> expressed concern for the island's northern coast from the <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Cuba" title="Provinces of Cuba">provinces</a> of <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> to <a href="/wiki/Camag%C3%BCey_Province" title="Camagüey Province">Camagüey</a>, and in particular the provinces of Matanzas and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_Province" title="Santa Clara Province">Las Villas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BahamasBatteredBlasts_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-BahamasBatteredBlasts-47">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[nb 5]</a></sup> Cuban radio alerted residents along the country's northern coast, potentially threatened by the hurricane, to take the necessary precautions in the event of an emergency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LashesNassauCuba_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-LashesNassauCuba-51">[46]</a></sup> Radio services in <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> alerted residents along the shores of <a href="/wiki/Pinar_del_R%C3%ADo_Province" title="Pinar del Río Province">Pinar del Río Province</a> of potentially dangerous storm surge, and urged immediate precautionary measures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BahamasBatteredBlasts_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-BahamasBatteredBlasts-47">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_Gulf_Coast">United States Gulf Coast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Betsy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: United States Gulf Coast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Watches_and_warnings">Watches and warnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Betsy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Watches and warnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">Tropical cyclone warnings and watches</a></div>
<p>Upon the operational <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">development</a> of Betsy into a tropical storm on August 27,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-10"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup> the San Juan Weather Bureau Office issued <a href="/wiki/Gale_warning" title="Gale warning">gale warnings</a> for Barbados, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="St. Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>. The weather office advised for small craft in the Windward and Leeward Islands to remain in port until the storm passed. These gale warnings were later expanded to include <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-1_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-1-4">[3]</a></sup> Midday on August 28, warnings were lowered for Barbados and St. Vincent and the Grenadines, and raised for areas of the northern Leeward Islands and later <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. Late that day, warnings in Dominica and Guadeloupe were discontinued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-2_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-2-9">[7]</a></sup> All warnings associated with the developing tropical cyclone were discontinued for a period of time on August 29,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-3_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-3-10">[8]</a></sup> as Betsy was pulling away from any landmasses. After the hurricane temporarily stalled and began to track westward on September 1,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-16"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> the Weather Bureau began to warn interests in the Bahamas. Though no warnings were specified, the tropical cyclone tracking agency forecasted winds of potentially <a href="/wiki/Beaufort_scale" title="Beaufort scale">hurricane-force</a> and strong surf to impact the Turks and Caicos Islands and Mayaguana;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-6_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-6-15">[12]</a></sup> such forecasts were changed after Betsy began tracking northwest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-10"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-17"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-7_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-7-16">[13]</a></sup> Threatening the coasts of <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Carolinas" title="The Carolinas">The Carolinas</a> on September 4,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-11"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> the Weather Bureau announced the possibility of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_watch" title="Hurricane watch">hurricane watch</a> for those coastal areas, but decided to delay the issuance of such watches due to Betsy's slow movement at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-13_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-13-20">[16]</a></sup> Nonetheless, the organization advised for small craft in coastal waters adjacent to the coast between Cape Kennedy to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sandy_Hook,_New_Jersey" title="Sandy Hook, New Jersey">Sandy Hook, New Jersey</a> to remain in port, and other small craft north of Miami, Florida and into Bahamian waters to exercise caution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-14_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-14-52">[47]</a></sup> As a result of Betsy executing a loop and beginning to tracking southwestward, these watches were never issued, however, the Weather Bureau advised extreme caution in several Bahamian islands, though once again no warnings were specified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-16_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-16-21">[17]</a></sup> However, general emergency hurricane warning was issued early on September 16 for islands in the northern Bahamas, as well as adjacent waters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-17_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-17-53">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-18_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-18-54">[49]</a></sup> Hurricane watches and gale warnings were also issued for surrounding islands at the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-18_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-18-54">[49]</a></sup> These warnings and watch products for the Bahamas held until late on September 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-24_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-24-23">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Early on September 6, as Betsy was tracking through the Bahamas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-11"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup> a hurricane watch and gale warning were issued for portions of the Southeastern Floridian coast from Cape Kennedy to <a href="/wiki/Key_West" title="Key West">Key West</a>. Late that day, however, areas of the watch zone from Palm Beach to Key West and Everglades City were upgraded to hurricane emergency warning status. Additional hurricane watches were hoisted for areas of Florida's western coast from <a href="/wiki/Everglades_City,_Florida" title="Everglades City, Florida">Everglades City</a> to <a href="/wiki/Punta_Gorda,_Florida" title="Punta Gorda, Florida">Punta Gorda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-18_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-18-54">[49]</a></sup> The following evening, the hurricane emergency warning zone was expanded to include areas of the east coast northward to <a href="/wiki/Fort_Pierce,_Florida" title="Fort Pierce, Florida">Fort Pierce</a> and on the west coast northward to <a href="/wiki/Venice,_Florida" title="Venice, Florida">Venice</a>. Gale warnings were also expanded to include coastal areas from <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a> to <a href="/wiki/St._Marks,_Florida" title="St. Marks, Florida">St. Marks</a>. Hurricane watches were similarly extended to include coastal regions of Florida from the boundaries of the hurricane warnings to <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach,_Florida" title="Daytona Beach, Florida">Daytona Beach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Keys_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Cedar Keys National Wildlife Refuge">Cedar Keys</a> on the peninsula's eastern and western coasts, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-24_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-24-23">[19]</a></sup> Once Betsy began moving through the peninsula, however, warning and watch products began to be discontinued by regions, with all products pertaining to Florida discontinued by midday on September 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-28_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-28-26">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-29_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-29-55">[50]</a></sup> After leaving the Florida area, the first hurricane watch pertaining to the Central Gulf Coast of the United States occurred late on September 8, when the Weather Bureau office in New Orleans issued a hurricane watch for coastal areas from <a href="/wiki/Matagorda_Bay" title="Matagorda Bay">Matagorda Bay</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River_Delta" title="Mississippi River Delta">Mississippi River Delta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-30_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-30-27">[23]</a></sup> Early the following day, hurricane emergency warnings were issued for areas stretching from <a href="/wiki/Galveston,_Texas" title="Galveston, Texas">Galveston, Texas</a> to the Mississippi River Delta and gale warnings elsewhere from <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Bay" title="Mobile Bay">Mobile Bay</a> to <a href="/wiki/Matagorda_Bay" title="Matagorda Bay">Matagorda Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-31_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-31-56">[51]</a></sup> Upon completing its northwestward recurvature, hurricane emergency warnings were shifted eastward to include areas from the mouth of the Mississippi River Delta to <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">Mobile, Alabama</a>. Gale warnings were effected by this change, and as such were also extended to include areas west of <a href="/wiki/Panama_City,_Florida" title="Panama City, Florida">Panama City, Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-33_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-33-57">[52]</a></sup> On September 9, hurricane warnings were once again extended eastward to <a href="/wiki/Pensacola,_Florida" title="Pensacola, Florida">Pensacola, Florida</a>, while they were lowered for the <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-34_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-34-58">[53]</a></sup> These warnings remained in effect until September 10, by which time Betsy had weakened sufficiently enough not to warrant such warnings and watches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADV-38_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADV-38-59">[54]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Betsy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Betsy_1965_rainfall.png"><img alt="Filled contoured map showing areas of North America; each contour represents a change of 3 in (75 mm) in precipitation totals." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="818" data-file-width="1121" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Betsy_1965_rainfall.png/275px-Betsy_1965_rainfall.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Betsy_1965_rainfall.png/413px-Betsy_1965_rainfall.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Betsy_1965_rainfall.png/550px-Betsy_1965_rainfall.png 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Betsy_1965_rainfall.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rainfall totals in the United States</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The effects of Hurricane Betsy were of far-reaching and unprecedented severity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-12"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-2_25-4"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2-25">[21]</a></sup> Though the extent of impacts were limited to the Bahamas and portions of the United States, the damage in these respective regions were considerable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-12"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Research_Division" title="Hurricane Research Division">Hurricane Research Division</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Oceanographic_and_Meteorological_Laboratory" title="Atlantic Oceanographic and Meteorological Laboratory">Atlantic Oceanographic and Meteorological Laboratory</a>, Betsy produced Category 3 winds (111 mph (179 km/h) or greater) in Southeastern Florida and Southeastern Louisiana.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChronologyHurricane_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-ChronologyHurricane-60">[55]</a></sup> However, winds of such intensity were also reported in the Bahamas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-13"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> The final, enumerated damage figure of $1.425 billion in damage costs made Betsy the first <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a> in the United States to accrue more than $1 billion in damage, unadjusted for <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeadliestTCs_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeadliestTCs-61">[56]</a></sup> For this reason, the tropical cyclone was nicknamed "Billion Dollar Betsy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USATodayBillionBetsy_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-USATodayBillionBetsy-62">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HurricaneScienceBetsy_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-HurricaneScienceBetsy-63">[58]</a></sup> The damage cost remained unsurpassed for four years until <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Camille" title="Hurricane Camille">Hurricane Camille</a> struck similar regions in <a href="/wiki/1969_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1969 Atlantic hurricane season">1969</a>. Betsy remains the 27th <a href="/wiki/List_of_costliest_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of costliest Atlantic hurricanes">costliest hurricane in U.S. history</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeadliestTCs_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-DeadliestTCs-61">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BillionDisasters_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-BillionDisasters-64">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IreneReport_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-IreneReport-65">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Bahamas">The Bahamas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Betsy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The Bahamas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During Betsy's initial approach of the Bahamian archipelago on September 2, strong surf and high swells were reported in the southeastern islands, though no damage was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyLashPittsburgh_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyLashPittsburgh-66">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsySkirt_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsySkirt-67">[62]</a></sup> Much of the damage inflicted to the Bahamas by Betsy occurred between September 6–8, when the tropical cyclone moved across the northern Bahamas as a Category 3 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-14"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-18"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup> The preceding track was similar to that of another <a href="/wiki/1929_Bahamas_hurricane" title="1929 Bahamas hurricane">major hurricane in</a> <a href="/wiki/1929_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1929 Atlantic hurricane season">1929</a>, which had also drastically curved southwestward before causing significant damage to the island group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WarningsExpected_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-WarningsExpected-39">[35]</a></sup> Likewise, Betsy was considered the worst hurricane to strike the region since then.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyClobber_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyClobber-68">[63]</a></sup> Stalling over the Bahamas for a period of time as it moved through the islands, several locations sustained the Betsy's effects for prolonged periods of time, despite the tropical cyclone's relatively small size.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-15"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-13"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup> Widespread <a href="/wiki/Power_outage" title="Power outage">power outage</a> and communication blackouts ensued, preventing the flow of reports between the northern Bahamas and other outlets as the storm took place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyHover_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyHover-69">[64]</a></sup> This included NASA communication centers in Cape Kennedy, which had lost contact with downrange missile tracking stations in the archipelago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LashingNassauFLSquall_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-LashingNassauFLSquall-70">[65]</a></sup> Over the duration of the hurricane, the lowest pressure measured was 961 mbar (hPa; 28.40 inHg) in <a href="/wiki/Dunmore_Town" title="Dunmore Town">Dunmore Town</a> on <a href="/wiki/Harbour_Island,_Bahamas" title="Harbour Island, Bahamas">Harbour Island</a>. However, no wind measurement was recorded alongside the pressure reading due to a resulting power failure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-16"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Offshore, the Dutch freighter Sarah Elizabeth was caught in rough seas and had lost control of its rudder while it was pulled by continuous wave action towards <a href="/wiki/Egg_Island_(Bahamas)" title="Egg Island (Bahamas)">Egg Island</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BahamasBatteredBlasts_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-BahamasBatteredBlasts-47">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LashingNassauFLSquall_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-LashingNassauFLSquall-70">[65]</a></sup> As a result, the ship's operators relayed a <a href="/wiki/SOS" title="SOS">SOS</a> signal, to which the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">United States Coast Guard</a> responded by dispatching a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cutter_(ship)" title="Cutter (ship)">cutter</a> and several merchant ships to assist in escorting the stricken freighter to safety. However, roughly five hours later the crew of the Sarah Elizabeth was able to navigate to safer waters within the <a href="/wiki/Great_Bahama_Canyon" title="Great Bahama Canyon">Providence Channel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LashingNassauFLSquall_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-LashingNassauFLSquall-70">[65]</a></sup> Two luxury <a href="/wiki/Yacht" title="Yacht">yachts</a> within the harbor were destroyed, with dozens of smaller craft damaged, as a result of the wind and waves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyClobber_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyClobber-68">[63]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Betsy_1965_Bahamas_and_Florida_Track.png"><img alt="Map showing the erratic track of a tropical cyclone as denoted by a thick black line. A gray, shaded region around the line indicates the width of the eye." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="438" data-file-width="555" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hurricane_Betsy_1965_Bahamas_and_Florida_Track.png/220px-Hurricane_Betsy_1965_Bahamas_and_Florida_Track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hurricane_Betsy_1965_Bahamas_and_Florida_Track.png/330px-Hurricane_Betsy_1965_Bahamas_and_Florida_Track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Hurricane_Betsy_1965_Bahamas_and_Florida_Track.png/440px-Hurricane_Betsy_1965_Bahamas_and_Florida_Track.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Betsy_1965_Bahamas_and_Florida_Track.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Track of Betsy through the Bahamas</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Passing to the north of <a href="/wiki/Nassau,_Bahamas" title="Nassau, Bahamas">Nassau</a>, Betsy caused considerable damage to the capital city and the rest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Providence_Island" title="New Providence Island">New Providence Island</a> as the hurricane's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eyewall" title="Eyewall">eyewall</a> stalled over the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-17"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyAimsFury_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyAimsFury-42">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BahamasBatteredBlasts_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-BahamasBatteredBlasts-47">[43]</a></sup> The last message received by the Miami Weather Bureau office from communication operators in Nassau during the storm was a report of 80 mph (130 km/h) winds and rough seas late on September 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyHover_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyHover-69">[64]</a></sup> The strong winds downed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_line" title="Power line">power lines</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyAimsFury_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyAimsFury-42">[38]</a></sup> trees,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BeadCuba_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-BeadCuba-46">[42]</a></sup> and destroyed homes, while the heavy rainfall, having accumulated over several days, flooding city streets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyAimsFury_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyAimsFury-42">[38]</a></sup> Other streets were littered with coconuts, palm fronds, and other debris blown or felled by the strong winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyClobber_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyClobber-68">[63]</a></sup> Heavy loss of shrubbery was also reported due to the storm's effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LashesNassauCuba_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-LashesNassauCuba-51">[46]</a></sup> A strong <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a> estimated at 10 ft (3.0 m) swept into the Bay Street waterfront shopping district, inundating the renowned shopping area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BeadCuba_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-BeadCuba-46">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LashingNassauFLSquall_70-3"><a href="#cite_note-LashingNassauFLSquall-70">[65]</a></sup> The local police detachment, which had been holed up within a waterfront barracks, was forced to take refuge in a nearby high school due to the storm surge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BahamasBatteredBlasts_47-4"><a href="#cite_note-BahamasBatteredBlasts-47">[43]</a></sup> Along the coast, 500 American tourists remained stranded in waterfront hotels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyClobber_68-3"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyClobber-68">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StalledBahamas_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-StalledBahamas-71">[66]</a></sup> Despite the severe effects, only one person died in the Nassau area after his ship was destroyed and capsized in Nassau Harbor; this would be the only fatality associated with Betsy in the Bahamas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-18"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>On <a href="/wiki/West_End,_Grand_Bahama" title="West End, Grand Bahama">West End</a> on <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bahama" title="Grand Bahama">Grand Bahama</a>, a weather station reported maximum sustained winds of 89 mph (143 km/h),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-19"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> with other locations elsewhere on the island experiencing gusts of at least 60 mph (97 km/h). However, no damage was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NassauTakesBeat_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-NassauTakesBeat-72">[67]</a></sup> Out of all the islands, the strongest winds were reported on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abaco_Island" title="Abaco Island">Abaco Island</a>, where areas were within Betsy's swath of <a href="/wiki/Beaufort_scale" title="Beaufort scale">hurricane-force</a> winds for over 20 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-1_3-14"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-1-3">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HurricaneCityAbaco_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-HurricaneCityAbaco-73">[68]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Green_Turtle_Cay" title="Green Turtle Cay">Green Turtle Cay</a>, a station clocked winds of 151 mph (243 km/h), well into Category 4 intensity on the modern-day Saffir–Simpson hurricane scale. Another station in <a href="/wiki/Hope_Town" title="Hope Town">Hope Town</a> measured a peak wind gust of 178 mph (286 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-20"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HurricaneCityBetsy_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-HurricaneCityBetsy-74">[69]</a></sup> The entirety of Hope Town was covered with sand to a depth of 2 ft (0.61 m), and the local harbor club was extensively damaged. Other docks were either damaged or completely destroyed. Though there was relatively little rainfall,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HurricaneBetsyRainsHelp_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-HurricaneBetsyRainsHelp-75">[70]</a></sup> coastal flooding damaged many houses to a point beyond repair. In <a href="/wiki/Marsh_Harbour" title="Marsh Harbour">Marsh Harbour</a>, a majority of homes were unroofed. Heavy crop and fruit tree losses were reported in Little and Northern Abaco, with damage enumerated at well over a million dollars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MajorHurricanesBahamas_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-MajorHurricanesBahamas-76">[71]</a></sup>In the southern Berry Islands, which experienced hurricane force winds for over 25 hours and the eye for 3 hours, all the islands suffered damage of some degree. Frazers Hog Cay had several houses badly damaged, one totally destroyed and the entire power distribution destroyed. Only Bird Cay, which had underground utilities, was able to restore electricity and water the next day. The harbor at Chub Cay was severely damaged. and would take months to repair.</p>
<p>Across the northern portion of <a href="/wiki/Eleuthera" title="Eleuthera">Eleuthera Island</a>, Betsy wrought considerable damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HurricaneCityEleuthera_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-HurricaneCityEleuthera-77">[72]</a></sup> Communications from the island's missile tracking center were lost, with the last transmitted message indicating winds of 130 mph (210 km/h) which subsequently destroyed an anemometer. A <a href="/wiki/Submarine_communications_cable" title="Submarine communications cable">submarine communications cable</a> connecting the missile tracking center to Cape Kennedy was cut by the strong wave action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150PoundsNassau_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-150PoundsNassau-78">[73]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Tarpum_Bay" title="Tarpum Bay">Tarpum Baya</a> police station sustained heavy damage after being hit by storm surge. Other coastal installments and property were severely damaged by the waves. The Glass Window Bridge was also damaged by the storm surge. Elsewhere, vehicles were damaged by fallen debris kicked up by the strong winds associated with Betsy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MajorHurricanesBahamas_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-MajorHurricanesBahamas-76">[71]</a></sup> Overall, Hurricane Betsy caused an estimated $14 million in damage across the Bahamas, primarily to crops. Insurance claims were estimated at $4 million. The low death toll from the hurricane was accredited by the United States Weather Bureau to the relatively low storm tide, which,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-21"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> although rough,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LashingNassauFLSquall_70-4"><a href="#cite_note-LashingNassauFLSquall-70">[65]</a></sup> was negligible in areas including in Nassau, and the heeding of posted hurricane warnings by the affected populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-22"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Florida">Florida</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Betsy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Florida">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Betsy_WSR-57_Miami.png"><img alt="Black and white radar image of a tropical cyclone; gray areas denote areas where rainfall is occurring. Although only a portion of the tropical cyclone is visible, rainbands and a central eye feature can be clearly made out." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="795" data-file-width="864" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Hurricane_Betsy_WSR-57_Miami.png/220px-Hurricane_Betsy_WSR-57_Miami.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Hurricane_Betsy_WSR-57_Miami.png/330px-Hurricane_Betsy_WSR-57_Miami.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Hurricane_Betsy_WSR-57_Miami.png/440px-Hurricane_Betsy_WSR-57_Miami.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Betsy_WSR-57_Miami.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/WSR-57" title="WSR-57">WSR-57</a> radar image of Betsy near Miami on September 8</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beginning on September 7, intermittent <a href="/wiki/Squall" title="Squall">squalls</a> associated with Betsy's outer <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">rainbands</a> began affecting the coast, producing gusts in excess of 60 mph (97 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LashingNassauFLSquall_70-5"><a href="#cite_note-LashingNassauFLSquall-70">[65]</a></sup> One of these squalls toppled trees and damaged awnings in <a href="/wiki/Stuart,_Florida" title="Stuart, Florida">Stuart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FloodingMainProblem_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FloodingMainProblem-79">[74]</a></sup> Early the following day, Betsy made landfall on the southeastern Florida coast near Key Largo with a strength equivalent to that of a Category 3 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_5-19"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-2_25-5"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2-25">[21]</a></sup> Intense winds were felt across the region, with the highest officially wind speed clocked at 125 mph (201 km/h) in <a href="/wiki/Big_Pine_Key,_Florida" title="Big Pine Key, Florida">Big Pine Key</a>; the same station also recorded the strongest gust documented while Betsy was over southern Florida at 165 mph (266 km/h). The lowest barometric pressure recorded was 952 mbar (hPa; 28.12 inHg) at a station in <a href="/wiki/Tavernier,_Florida" title="Tavernier, Florida">Tavernier</a> while it was within the eye of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-23"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StormData_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-StormData-80">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>The strong winds knocked down utility poles, causing widespread power outage and a telecommunications blackout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyMuddy_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyMuddy-81">[76]</a></sup> At one point, an estimated 25,000 telephones were knocked out of service, with half of the central <a href="/wiki/Telephone_exchange" title="Telephone exchange">telephone exchange</a> operating on emergency backup power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FloodingMainProblem_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-FloodingMainProblem-79">[74]</a></sup> Some <a href="/wiki/Transformer" title="Transformer">transformers</a> that were blown down sparked localized fires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyMuddy_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyMuddy-81">[76]</a></sup> One person was killed after being electrocuted by a fallen power line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WallOfWater_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-WallOfWater-82">[77]</a></sup> The blackouts cut electric service to 80 percent of customers in the Miami and Fort Lauderdale areas. House trailers were smashed by flying debris in the same areas. Several roads were blocked by debris thrown by the wind. <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 1 in Florida">U.S. Highway 1</a> in <a href="/wiki/Florida_City,_Florida" title="Florida City, Florida">Florida</a> was cut off by fallen telephone poles, preventing land access from the mainland to the Florida Keys. Similarly, numerous portions of the <a href="/wiki/Tamiami_Trail" title="Tamiami Trail">Tamiami Trail</a> were blocked by fallen trees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FloridaBatteredHighWind_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FloridaBatteredHighWind-83">[78]</a></sup> A person was killed after a prostrated tree fell, crushing the individual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyTurnsFury_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyTurnsFury-84">[79]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami International Airport</a>, two twin-engine cargo craft were blown off the airport's perimeter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FloodingMainProblem_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-FloodingMainProblem-79">[74]</a></sup> Heavy agricultural losses resulted from the strong winds as well. Approximately 25 to 50 percent of Florida's citrus crop was damaged after being blown down by strong winds. In addition, 90 percent of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dade_County,_Florida" title="Dade County, Florida">Dade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">Broward</a> counties' avocado crop,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-24"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> valued at $2 million, was destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FloridaBatteredHighWind_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-FloridaBatteredHighWind-83">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Much of the damage inflicted in the state was caused by an unusually strong storm surge, which inundated the coastal and low-lying areas of Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-25"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> Although the strongest storm surge was positioned north of the eye, away from the more densely populated regions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Miami" title="Greater Miami">Greater Miami</a>, an abnormally high storm tide still prevailed and caused extensive damage along the southern coast of the peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HurricaneBetsySwamps_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-HurricaneBetsySwamps-85">[80]</a></sup> Northerly winds well in advance of Betsy's landfall forced water from Florida Bay onto the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys" title="Florida Keys">Florida Keys</a>, and the resulting damage was then further exacerbated when southerly winds during and after the hurricane's approach forced water from the Atlantic onto the isolated Keys. Though storm surge was estimated to have peaked along the coast of North Key Largo at 9 ft (2.7 m), a measurement of 7.7 ft (2.3 m) in Tavernier was the highest measured total. However, a <a href="/wiki/High_water_mark" title="High water mark">high water mark</a> of 9 ft (2.7 m) on a highway west of <a href="/wiki/Sugarloaf_Key" title="Sugarloaf Key">Sugarloaf Key</a> indicated that such estimations in North Key Largo were valid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-26"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> The strong storm surge caused severe <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beach_erosion" title="Beach erosion">beach erosion</a>, mostly to areas south of <a href="/wiki/Clearwater,_Florida" title="Clearwater, Florida">Clearwater</a> on the state's western coast while Betsy was traversing the Gulf of Mexico. In Fort Pierce, the waves washed away up to 10 ft (3.0 m) of beach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FloodingMainProblem_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-FloodingMainProblem-79">[74]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Betsy_Key_West_Street_Flooding.jpg"><img alt="Slightly elevated photo taken in the middle of a flooded street. Palm trees, utility poles, and residences are visible on both the left and right sides of the street." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="861" data-file-width="1280" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Hurricane_Betsy_Key_West_Street_Flooding.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Betsy_Key_West_Street_Flooding.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Hurricane_Betsy_Key_West_Street_Flooding.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Betsy_Key_West_Street_Flooding.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Hurricane_Betsy_Key_West_Street_Flooding.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Betsy_Key_West_Street_Flooding.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Betsy_Key_West_Street_Flooding.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Street flooding in Key West</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Coastal flooding in the Upper Keys was severe, with areas being inundated under several feet of seawater. Along the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Beach,_Florida" title="Miami Beach, Florida">Miami Beach</a> waterfront, a storm tide measuring 6.1 ft (1.9 m) caused extensive damage to shoreline property along <a href="/wiki/Biscayne_Bay" title="Biscayne Bay">Biscayne Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StormData_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-StormData-80">[75]</a></sup> Eight people on the beach were injured, primarily due to flying glass shards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FloridaShambles_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FloridaShambles-86">[81]</a></sup> Roads were inundated, with water exceeding the first floor heights of some buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StormData_80-2"><a href="#cite_note-StormData-80">[75]</a></sup> As a result of the waves and wind, three barges were torn out of their moorings, and later drifted downwind before severing a portion of the <a href="/wiki/Rickenbacker_Causeway" title="Rickenbacker Causeway">Rickenbacker Causeway</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FloridaBatteredHighWind_83-2"><a href="#cite_note-FloridaBatteredHighWind-83">[78]</a></sup> rendering it impassable and isolating <a href="/wiki/Key_Biscayne" title="Key Biscayne">Key Biscayne</a> from the mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyTurnsFury_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyTurnsFury-84">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HurricaneFloodsMiami_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-HurricaneFloodsMiami-87">[82]</a></sup> Along the waterfront, the waves blew into hotels and shoreline residences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyMuddy_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyMuddy-81">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Offshore, the strong waves caused a freighter to run aground near Palm Beach, and nine people became stranded in <a href="/wiki/Houseboat" title="Houseboat">houseboats</a> near a mangrove island in Biscayne Bay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyChurnsHavoc_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyChurnsHavoc-88">[83]</a></sup> Another cargo ship, the <i>Panamanian</i>, ran aground within <a href="/wiki/Lake_Worth_Inlet" title="Lake Worth Inlet">Lake Worth Inlet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HurricaneFloodsMiami_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-HurricaneFloodsMiami-87">[82]</a></sup> At Key Largo, a 50 ft (15 m) sailboat was blown out of the water onto an adjacent neighborhood. Elsewhere in Key Largo, homes were unroofed by the strong winds, with other buildings damaged by flying debris.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyChurnsHavoc_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyChurnsHavoc-88">[83]</a></sup> Water forced into the <a href="/wiki/Miami_River_(Florida)" title="Miami River (Florida)">Miami River</a> caused it to overflow its banks and spread inland for several city blocks in Miami. In the Miami area, Betsy caused the most severe seawater inundation since a <a href="/wiki/1926_Miami_hurricane" title="1926 Miami hurricane">major hurricane</a> struck in <a href="/wiki/1926_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1926 Atlantic hurricane season">1926</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsyMuddy_81-3"><a href="#cite_note-BetsyMuddy-81">[76]</a></sup> this record was attributed to the highest storm surge reported in as many years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HurricaneFloodsMiami_87-2"><a href="#cite_note-HurricaneFloodsMiami-87">[82]</a></sup> A 5 mi (8.0 km) section of <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_A1A" title="Florida State Road A1A">State Road A1A</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsySlamsIntoSE_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-BetsySlamsIntoSE-89">[84]</a></sup> which runs adjacent to Miami and the nearby beach, was blocked by sand dunes piled inland by the strong winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FloridaBatteredHighWind_83-3"><a href="#cite_note-FloridaBatteredHighWind-83">[78]</a></sup> The high tide also washed out a some portions of the road between Fort Lauderdale and <a href="/wiki/Pompano_Beach,_Florida" title="Pompano Beach, Florida">Pompano Beach</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BetsySpokesmanReviewFlorida_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-BetsySpokesmanReviewFlorida-45">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Precipitation was localized, albeit heavy, in South Florida. Rainfall peaked at 11.80 in (300 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Plantation_Key,_Florida" title="Plantation Key, Florida">Plantation Key</a> on September 8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-27"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FLRain_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FLRain-90">[85]</a></sup> The weather station in Big Pine Key observed the second highest state rainfall total at 10.52 in (267 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-28"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup> Elsewhere, rainfall spread as far northward as <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay" title="Tampa Bay">Tampa Bay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPCRain_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-WPCRain-29">[25]</a></sup> Although intense, the rains helped partially alleviate a concurrent <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">drought</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Everglades" title="Everglades">Everglades</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HurricaneBetsyRainsHelp_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-HurricaneBetsyRainsHelp-75">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FuriousBetsyBatters_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FuriousBetsyBatters-91">[86]</a></sup> No damage was reported in association with the rainfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-2_25-6"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2-25">[21]</a></sup> A total of three <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a> formed in association with Betsy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StormData_80-3"><a href="#cite_note-StormData-80">[75]</a></sup> of which two occurred while the major hurricane was landfalling in South Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-2_25-7"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2-25">[21]</a></sup> On September 8, a tornado developed and track near <a href="/wiki/Marathon,_Florida" title="Marathon, Florida">Marathon</a>, while another occurred near Big Pine Key; both tornadoes caused no reported damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StormData_80-4"><a href="#cite_note-StormData-80">[75]</a></sup> However, a <a href="/wiki/Waterspout" title="Waterspout">waterspout</a> formed near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Walton_Beach" title="Fort Walton Beach">Fort Walton Beach</a> off the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Panhandle" title="Florida Panhandle">Florida Panhandle</a> the following day and later destroyed a marina with twelve boats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCR-2_25-8"><a href="#cite_note-TCR-2-25">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StormData_80-5"><a href="#cite_note-StormData-80">[75]</a></sup> The relatively low number of tornadoes that formed as a result of Betsy was due to the anomalously rapid forward motion that Betsy traveled at during its traverse of the Florida peninsula and the Gulf of Mexico. Overall, five people were killed in the state,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StormData_80-6"><a href="#cite_note-StormData-80">[75]</a></sup> and damage totaled $139 million, primarily due to the strong storm surge generated by Betsy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR-Season_2-29"><a href="#cite_note-MWR-Season-2">[1]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gulf_of_Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Betsy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Gulf of Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HurricaneBetsyFloodingAirForceONE.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1302" data-file-width="2000" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/HurricaneBetsyFloodingAirForceONE.jpg/220px-HurricaneBetsyFloodingAirForceONE.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/HurricaneBetsyFloodingAirForceONE.jpg/330px-HurricaneBetsyFloodingAirForceONE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/HurricaneBetsyFloodingAirForceONE.jpg/440px-HurricaneBetsyFloodingAirForceONE.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HurricaneBetsyFloodingAirForceONE.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aerial view of flooding in New Orleans</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NOLA9thFloodedBetsy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="917" data-file-width="696" height="290" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/NOLA9thFloodedBetsy.jpg/220px-NOLA9thFloodedBetsy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/NOLA9thFloodedBetsy.jpg/330px-NOLA9thFloodedBetsy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/NOLA9thFloodedBetsy.jpg/440px-NOLA9thFloodedBetsy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NOLA9thFloodedBetsy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flooding in the Lower 9th Ward of New Orleans after Betsy</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Eight offshore oil platforms were destroyed during Betsy, with others experiencing damage. A <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Shell</a> oil platform off the Mouth of the Mississippi river was not seen again. The oil rig Maverick, owned by future president <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>'s Zapata corporation also disappeared during the cyclone. It was insured by <a href="/wiki/Lloyd%27s_of_London" title="Lloyd's of London">Lloyd's of London</a> for US$5.7 million (1965 dollars).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana">Louisiana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Betsy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Louisiana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
